<div id="review_1409828102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409828102" />
    <a title="LuAnn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13131441-luann"><img alt="LuAnn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548167513p2/13131441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409828102?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LuAnn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LuAnn" href="/user/show/13131441-luann">LuAnn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13131441-luann?shelf=bookbooks">bookbooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13131441-luann?shelf=2015-challenge">2015-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409828102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4314642092389608757"> I did not want to like The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto. It's an odd title. (I like cozy mysteries, so I know odd titles!) Mitch Ablom is a famous author. His books have been on national best-seller lists. So the expectations go through the roof and I didn't think his book could live up to that.<br/><br/>Now, I am most happy to report that Frankie Presto started growing on me from the first note. And there is no choice between first-person and third-person narration, because Music is itself the narrat</span>
  <span id="freeText4314642092389608757" style="display:none"> I did not want to like The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto. It's an odd title. (I like cozy mysteries, so I know odd titles!) Mitch Ablom is a famous author. His books have been on national best-seller lists. So the expectations go through the roof and I didn't think his book could live up to that.<br /><br />Now, I am most happy to report that Frankie Presto started growing on me from the first note. And there is no choice between first-person and third-person narration, because Music is itself the narrator.<br /><br />And talk about humble beginnings. Frankie was born in the upstairs area of a church that was being looted and burned by soldiers in a war. His mother sings him a song to keep him quiet so the soldiers will not find them too quickly. The song stays will him his entire life. Literally...it keeps showing up.<br /><br />His mother dies and a nun changes clothes with the mother and then takes Frankie away from the church and raises him as her own. Until she can't deal with the stress of single motherhood (it's NOT for sissies, that's for sure) and she throws him away. Much of his childhood is spent with the man that rescued him as a toddler, believing this man to be his father.<br /><br />His 'father' runs afoul of the Spanish government and is taken away to prison. He pays the boy's blind guitar teacher to spirit the boy to the United States. Dirty dealing on a 3rd person's part leaves the boy alone on the docks in England, playing for money to eat. There he runs into a down-on-his-inspiration jazz musician and agrees to accompany him to America.<br /> <br />I absolutely ADORED the part where he subs for Elvis, but that's all I'm going to say about that. <br /><br />The method of interspersing the chapters about Frankie's story with interviews of famous musicians at Frankie's funeral brings an engaging angle to the overall story. I'm also glad that the full story gives us information on what Frankie was doing in all those "lost years". It was also gratifying to know that this famous musical character, after his years of getting caught up in the pitfalls of fame, was able to get a final, satisfying resolution to his life.<br /><br />So, what's the deal with the 'magic' in the strings? Does it refer solely to Frankie's musical talent? No. The guitar that has been with him the majority of his life from the age of 9 had strings that had been provided to his mother, if I remember correctly, by a gypsy family to whom she had shown charity before Frankie was born.<br /><br /> Music can have charms to tame not only the savage breast, but one of these charmed strings turns blue each time Frankie comes closer to his real purpose. It then breaks. Despite the decreasing number of strings, Frankie continues to make incredible music with the guitar given him by his beloved first music teacher. (I must admit, to my chagrin, that I thought the cover was strange at first. And then, I understood.)<br /><br />Maybe that's the real jewel of this story, that no matter our circumstances, we can still fulfill our destinies. To quote Peter Pan, "All you need is faith and trust...and a little bit of pixie dust."<br /><br />So here I am, having read The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto. It was an immensely satisfying read. My heart ached at the story of his birth. I was outraged at the events surrounding his leaving Spain at a young age. I did kind of want to slap him upside the head when he started heading down the wrong path, like I would do for a brother or a good friend. And I did a little mental 'fist pump' at his final performance.<br /><br />If you have a beating heart, The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto will resonate in unison with the beat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4314642092389608757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425187286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3884839569469256807">Tears. So many tears.<br/><br/>The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto is a tragedy. I don't care how it ends, or what you think of it. It is tragic. I cried. I connected to Frankie, especially as a child. As readers, we witness homeless little Little Frankie Presto become a musical legend. I've never seen a character be dealt such horrible cards from the get-go. Still, he is hopeful and there is a light in his eyes. We then get to watch that light fade as he overcomes these obstacles. Blow after blow, Franci</span>
  <span id="freeText3884839569469256807" style="display:none">Tears. So many tears.<br /><br />The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto is a tragedy. I don't care how it ends, or what you think of it. It is tragic. I cried. I connected to Frankie, especially as a child. As readers, we witness homeless little Little Frankie Presto become a musical legend. I've never seen a character be dealt such horrible cards from the get-go. Still, he is hopeful and there is a light in his eyes. We then get to watch that light fade as he overcomes these obstacles. Blow after blow, Francisco fights his way through life, meeting legendary historical musicians and creating a name for himself. (This man will have at least three names by the time this book is over.)<br /><br /><b>Francisco is not your average human being.</b> This is the only part I had trouble with. (I'm looking at you, everyone who couldn't deal with Music being the narrator. C'mon. It was like any other narrator.)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Frankie should've died. He should've been blind. He should've been many things that he wasn't. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But Frankie had a handful of miracles and he continued to beat the odds.<br /><br />I honestly didn't expect to like this book. I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2331.Mitch_Albom" title="Mitch Albom" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mitch Albom</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6900.Tuesdays_with_Morrie" title="Tuesdays with Morrie by Mitch Albom" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tuesdays with Morrie</a> but in general, none of his other books have drawn my interest. I am so very glad I got the opportunity to read this.<br /><br />It reads fast and I really couldn't put it down.<br /><br />Note: I received this remarkable novel through a Goodreads first reads contest. I am very glad that I did.</span>

<div id="review_1598486815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1598486815" />
    <a title="Aoife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife"><img alt="Aoife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514771423p2/16768476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1598486815?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife">Aoife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=literary">literary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1598486815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17967001942503535546">4.5 stars<br/><br/>There's something about Mitch Albom's writing that is so beautiful and magical, I could just bathe in all the words. <br/><br/>Frankie Presto was once one of the greats and rubbed shoulders with Elvis, Hank Williams, Django Reinhardt and Darlene Love.He was born in the middle of Franco's dictatorship of Spain and found his way through America. The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto starts with the death of Frankie and we make our way to the start of his story, who he was, how he learned to play the </span>
  <span id="freeText17967001942503535546" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />There's something about Mitch Albom's writing that is so beautiful and magical, I could just bathe in all the words. <br /><br />Frankie Presto was once one of the greats and rubbed shoulders with Elvis, Hank Williams, Django Reinhardt and Darlene Love.He was born in the middle of Franco's dictatorship of Spain and found his way through America. The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto starts with the death of Frankie and we make our way to the start of his story, who he was, how he learned to play the guitar like he did and who gifted him the magic strings that turn blue when he changes someone's life with his music.<br /><br />I think this is a must-read for anyone who loved The Book Thief. Instead of Germany in WW2, we have Spain in the late 1940s. Instead of book-loving Liesel, we have music-loving Francisco. And instead of being told by Death, Frankie's story is told by Music. Yeah, you read that right. Music is a being, an all-seeing entity in this book. It gives a piece of him to newborns to create music during their lives and when they die, it takes it back.<br /><br /><i>“All humans are musical.<br />Why else would the Lord give you a beating heart?”</i><br /><br />I'm not huge into music but even I was fascinated the way Mitch Albom was able to place Frankie Presto into the time of Elvis and Johnny Cash and weave him into the lives of other famous musicians. Presto meets Django Reinhardt, Hank Williams, Elvis, Darlene Love, Roger McGuin, Lyle Lovett, Tony Bennett over the course of his life and we find out how he rose and fell in the limelight and why he stepped out of it altogether but was never forgotten by fellow artists and fans of great music.<br /><br />This was such an amazing story of an amazing life, and you would almost believe Presto was a real person in this era. You're almost sad that he wasn't a real person! There were real heartbreaking moments in this one - Francisco looking for Baffa at the factory, when he meets his aunt and screeched 'momma', his lost moments at Woodstock, the last song he sings to Aurora...there are so many wonderful moments that really gripped me. <br /><br />I'm taking away a .5 of a star just because near the end some of Frankie's actions annoyed me a bit and I was ready for the story to start winding up. But I thoroughly enjoyed this one for the most part and Mitch Albom has proven to be again that he can cast me under a spell with his words. Wonderful. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17967001942503535546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1418279889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418279889" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3973707-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280498562p2/3973707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418279889?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/3973707-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418279889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12862096878043123055">Mitch Albom has a flair for writing warm, personal stories that have a freshness and depth to them. "The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto" is no exception. Readers don't need to have an affection for or a deep interest in music to see and feel the connections in this book, but it probably adds a bit of spark if there's some kind of appreciation for music.<br/><br/>This story tells Frankie's life and the impact it had on people close to him, and those who were at a distance. Not only does the story explore </span>
  <span id="freeText12862096878043123055" style="display:none">Mitch Albom has a flair for writing warm, personal stories that have a freshness and depth to them. "The Magic Strings of Frankie Presto" is no exception. Readers don't need to have an affection for or a deep interest in music to see and feel the connections in this book, but it probably adds a bit of spark if there's some kind of appreciation for music.<br /><br />This story tells Frankie's life and the impact it had on people close to him, and those who were at a distance. Not only does the story explore the importance and magic of music, it wraps up a deep and abiding love which isn't perfect but doesn't pretend or assume it is, in music's embrace, as well. Every aspect, positive or negative, triumph or defeat, is somehow connected to the music in Frankie's soul. Music is one of the narrators of Frankie's life story, as a matter of fact. <br /><br />Many people tell Frankie's story - from a variety of musicians (most that people will recognize), to Music, to an unknown narrator who fills in some blanks in Frankie's timeline. Usually, the story flows well and the change in narrators is fluid and easy to follow. Once, somewhere in the middle of Frankie's story, I stumbled a little with a time change, but quickly caught up with where I should be.<br /><br />I enjoyed this uplifting story about how a boy grows into a man and discovers he possesses magic guitar strings and finally realizes what those magic strings mean. It was a fun yet fulfilling story that gave me plenty to think (and feel) about without being preachy or over-done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12862096878043123055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2602803381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2602803381" />
    <a title="Fatma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3562540-fatma"><img alt="Fatma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602516692p2/3562540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2602803381?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fatma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fatma" href="/user/show/3562540-fatma">Fatma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961903743?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/33653733-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33653733-lori?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961903743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17411451026586355930">Have you ever entertained the idea of joining a band? According to the Narrator of Mitch Albom’s new book, “The Magic Strings Of Frankie Presto,” we all join a band in life. And it will affect you as much as you affect it! That “Narrator” is “Music” itself and it highlights the fictional life of Frankie Presto - an Elvis look-alike who was orphaned in a burning church and raised by a blind guitar teacher. Blending spiritual teachings with musical disciplines Albom weaves Frankie’s life with othe</span>
  <span id="freeText17411451026586355930" style="display:none">Have you ever entertained the idea of joining a band? According to the Narrator of Mitch Albom’s new book, “The Magic Strings Of Frankie Presto,” we all join a band in life. And it will affect you as much as you affect it! That “Narrator” is “Music” itself and it highlights the fictional life of Frankie Presto - an Elvis look-alike who was orphaned in a burning church and raised by a blind guitar teacher. Blending spiritual teachings with musical disciplines Albom weaves Frankie’s life with other great musicians such as Duke Ellington, Wynton Marsalis, Darlene Love, Lyle Lovett and others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17411451026586355930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1943756600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1943756600" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7891507-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443344607p2/7891507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1943756600?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/7891507-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943756600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13513946216124458241">Mitch Albom is most definitely my go-to author for feel-good stories. After the last book I read, I needed a spiritual cleansing. This one did the trick.<br/><br/>I've not read everything Albom has written but I've read enough to know that this is his worst so far. But Albom's worst exceeds some author's best - I gave it three stars so that's saying something. <br/><br/>This is the Story of Frankie Presto from his birth to death as narrated by friends who came to his funeral and the entity known as...nope, not the </span>
  <span id="freeText13513946216124458241" style="display:none">Mitch Albom is most definitely my go-to author for feel-good stories. After the last book I read, I needed a spiritual cleansing. This one did the trick.<br /><br />I've not read everything Albom has written but I've read enough to know that this is his worst so far. But Albom's worst exceeds some author's best - I gave it three stars so that's saying something. <br /><br />This is the Story of Frankie Presto from his birth to death as narrated by friends who came to his funeral and the entity known as...nope, not the Grim Reaper,but close - it's Music. Yup, Music gives a piece of himself to those who grab for it at birth and Music collects it back at death. With Music being the narrator, there was a lot of music-speak like "we will continue this story in allegro". What? Anyhow, this was the star-sucker for me. Aside from Music, the story itself was pretty good. Not as sad for me as they usually are but I wasn't looking for totally heart-wrenching, just something to make me feel like the world isn't evil.<br /><br />If you've never read Mitch Albom, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6900.Tuesdays_with_Morrie" title="Tuesdays with Morrie by Mitch Albom" rel="nofollow noopener">Tuesdays with Morrie</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3431.The_Five_People_You_Meet_in_Heaven" title="The Five People You Meet in Heaven by Mitch Albom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Five People You Meet in Heaven</a> first. They are really good. This was OK but I wouldn't recommend starting with this one </span>
  <a data-text-id="13513946216124458241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1446644423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446644423" />
    <a title="Joanna Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34018865-joanna-marie"><img alt="Joanna Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547092010p2/34018865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446644423?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna Marie" href="/user/show/34018865-joanna-marie">Joanna Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062294418" href="/book/show/25142924-the-magic-strings-of-frankie-presto">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446644423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5452507250728892538"><b>Everybody joins a band in this life.</b><br/><br/>huhu mitch albom is always an inspiration. his books always make me sigh. twas said that this is his most sweeping novel yet and i agree. no words can describe how beautiful and profound this is. all his books are actually but i must say this, by far, is my most favorite next to Tuesdays with Morrie. The book kicked off with Music's narration and right there and then I already knew that this book will grip my heart tightly ❤</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('caTofMWNomOGk167TLMJ4+nang02JdGZJCZqM8pLH9mNd2Qnyc8ULsbMUw8daEI01Wvs+aMiixwg+TyaPx7fxQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nRqwrtqvaPtKD/jbLHbFCLdhuU7TBjYeLoRUziGB3kdhyTz11u3etgpQ9W99rY7fi9DLukYBbJsqWwJn1NQeWw==')})
  }

He won a Rhodes Scholarship to Oxford, then returned to Canada and enrolled in Wycliffe College, the bastion of Anglican evangelicalism. Ordained to the ministry, Tom Harpur served for a number of years in his own parish before seeking a wider ministry in the world of mass media.\n\nIn 1971, Tom Harpur joined the Toronto Star as the religion editor and over a number of years reported on and met many important figures from Pope John Paul and Mother Teresa to the Dali Lama, Jean Vanier, and Billy Graham. Here are fascinating anecdotes about these influential people and compelling accounts of the author\'s travels around the globe. \n\nPerhaps Tom Harpur\'s most intimate book, Born Again is a important work of spiritual insight, revelation and renewal.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11833623190624973255\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n For anyone who has felt, even for a moment, the ‘missingness’ of an unlived life and wondered what to do about it.   When Lindy’s husband discovers that she has been living a secret life as a burlesque dancer, all while he has been home watching football, the glitter hits the fan. Perimenopause (whatever that is) does not help matters, and Lindy finds herself in increasingly compromising situations: there is Thor, the stuntman from Texas, Satya with the dreadlocks and camper-van, beautiful Adam, and the Crazy.  In the midst of a hot flush, Lindy remembers her destiny (bestowed on her by Father Ignatius at Catholic school when she was fifteen years old) to save the world. So, on her fifty-first birthday, she tells her husband that she can no longer be married. She needs to find her Big Life, the one that doesn’t include a picket-fence house in the suburbs with a minivan in the driveway. Since her husband is, above all, a practical man, he suggests that she go for a walk to think about things before making any final decisions.  Forgetting that she doesn’t like walking, Lindy heads to Northern Spain with her purple backpack, Petunia. With blistered toes and a swollen ankle, she stomps along the sacred soil of the Camino de Santiago in search of God (if he exists), forgiveness (if that is possible), and herself (whomever the hell that is). With no guidebook and no sense of direction, she gets lost. Very lost. In that lostness, she is forced to stare the serpent in the eye, have it out with Jesus, and face her naked truth.  Told with audacious honesty, The Common Wife is the irreverent memoir of one woman\'s pilgrimage to the Ends of the Earth. Think Bridget Jones’s Diary, combined with Eat, Pray, Love and Wild. Add a bunch of pilgrims, a toolbox filled with glitter, Satan on a mountaintop and pole-dancing Jesus.
